    <script src="/templates/jsp/pb2/js/plugin/thiss-ds.js" nonce="6baf9fad70584ad3bd44be1f041e9620"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="6baf9fad70584ad3bd44be1f041e9620">

        function getParameter(parameterName) {
            let result = null,
                tmp = [];
            location.search
                .substr(1)
                .split("&")
                .forEach(function (item) {
                    tmp = item.split("=");
                    if (tmp[0] === parameterName) result = tmp[1];
                });
            return result;
        }

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            queryParamsDelimiter: encodeURIComponent('?'),

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                let redirectURL = getParameter('redirectUri');
                if(redirectURL == null){
                    redirectURL = encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
                }
                if(redirectURL.indexOf('saml_referrer') < 0){
                    redirectURL += encodeURIComponent(((redirectURL.indexOf(this.queryParamsDelimiter) !== -1) ? '&' : '?') + 'saml_referrer');
                }
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + redirectURL;
            },
            retrieveEntity: function () {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // get the results
                            var results = res.data;
                            return resolve(results);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('retrieve entity error: ' + err);
                        });
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage duo to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {doi: doi, entityid: entityId, entityTitle: entityTitle, eventGroupKey: '932b2855-12d6-41cf-9d85-3f559d5c645d'}

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (let i in allSsoInstitutions) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();
                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err){
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

                     <p>Institute for Applied Materials, Karlsruhe Institute of Technology, Hermann-von-Helmholtz-Platz 1, 76344 Eggenstein-Leopoldshafen, Germany</p><a class="moreInfoLink" href="/authored-by/H%C3%A4ringer/Marcel">Search for more papers by this author</a></div></span><span class="accordion-tabbed__tab-mobile  accordion__closed"><a href="/authored-by/Neusser/Gregor" class="author-name accordion-tabbed__control" data-id="a4" data-db-target-for="a4" aria-controls="a4" aria-haspopup="true" id="a4_Ctrl" role="button"><span>Gregor Neusser</span><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-section_arrow_d"></i></a><span class="comma-separator">,&nbsp;</span><div class="author-info accordion-tabbed__content" data-db-target-of="a4" aria-labelledby="a4_Ctrl" role="region" id="a4">

   <div class="abstract-group  metis-abstract">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" id="abstract-graphical-en" style="">
         <h2 id="d118525112" class="article-section__header section__title graphical abstractlang_en graphical">Graphical Abstract</h2>
         <div class="graphical-abstract">
            <p>The morphology of NVP/C composites, used in cathodes for sodium-ion batteries, is investigated by combining advanced imaging techniques, nanostructure characterization, and stochastic 3D modeling. The effect of varying the amount of carbon is studied by means of the presented data-driven modeling approach.
            </p><figure>
               <div class="center graphic__image"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/cf72e6f1-6e8b-4462-b0bf-209b75df4099/batt202300409-toc-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/cf72e6f1-6e8b-4462-b0bf-209b75df4099/batt202300409-toc-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/552b838b-6d59-495d-9154-fec1b1cdfd08/batt202300409-toc-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/cf72e6f1-6e8b-4462-b0bf-209b75df4099/batt202300409-toc-0001-m.jpg" alt="Description unavailable" title="Description unavailable" loading="lazy"></picture></a><p class="caption-style"></p>
               </div>
            </figure>
            <p></p>
            </div>
      </section>
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en" style="">
         <h2 id="d118525157" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>A data-driven modeling approach is presented to quantify the influence of morphology on effective properties in nanostructured sodium vanadium phosphate <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0001" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/4d50449b-0102-4493-9816-5cf9a337ef4f/batt202300409-math-0001.png">
/ carbon composites (NVP/C), which are used as cathode material in sodium-ion batteries. This approach is based on the combination of advanced imaging techniques, experimental nanostructure characterization and stochastic modeling of the 3D nanostructure consisting of NVP, carbon and pores. By 3D imaging and subsequent post-processing involving image segmentation, the spatial distribution of NVP is resolved in 3D, and the spatial distribution of carbon and pores is resolved in 2D. Based on this information, a parametric stochastic model, specifically a Pluri-Gaussian model, is calibrated to the 3D morphology of the nanostructured NVP/C particles. Model validation is performed by comparing the nanostructure of simulated NVP/C composites with image data in terms of morphological descriptors which have not been used for model calibration. Finally, the stochastic model is used for predictive simulation to quantify the effect of varying the amount of carbon while keeping the amount of NVP constant. The presented methodology opens new possibilities for a ressource-efficient optimization of the morphology of NVP/C particles by modeling and simulation.</p>
            </div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="batt202300409-sec-0001">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="batt202300409-sec-0001-title"> Introduction</h2>
         
         <p>For energy storage in consumer electronics, electric vehicles and stationary applications, lithium-ion batteries allowing for high energy densities are the dominant technology nowadays.<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0001_R_d118525043e425" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Nat. Energy">1</a></sup></span> Due to the potential increase in the price of lithium, the toxicity of cobalt required for the widely used active material <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0002" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/4f682884-e801-4eb3-8c99-5ce52b6bf828/batt202300409-math-0002.png">
 (NMC), and the limited supply of both, lithium and cobalt,<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0002" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0002_R_d118525043e430" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2 - Joule">2</a></sup></span> alternative battery chemistries are explored. Among these alternatives, sodium-ion batteries<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0003_R_d118525043e433" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - Chem. Soc. Rev.">3</a></sup></span> are promising candidates. This requires the manufacturing of appropriate electrode materials for an optimized performance of these batteries.</p>
         
         <p>A popular active material for cathodes in sodium-ion batteries is <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0003" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/63af8cfa-e1b4-42d2-ac53-bd31041f5183/batt202300409-math-0003.png">
 (NVP).<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0004_R_d118525043e441" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Nanoscale">4</a></sup></span> The main benefit of this material arises from its high energy density, cycle stability, and rate capability.<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0005_R_d118525043e444" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - J. Energy Chem.">5</a></sup></span> To obtain a sufficient conductivity of the cathodes, NVP/carbon composite coatings are applied.<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0006_R_d118525043e447" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - ACS Appl. Energ. Mater.">6</a>-<a href="#batt202300409-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0008_R_d118525043e447" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Dalton Trans.">8</a></sup></span> The performance of the cell strongly depends on effective properties of the composite material at the nano-scale, which–in turn–are influenced by the spatial distribution of the constituents of this composite material. Optimizing these electrode materials requires a comprehensive understanding of relationships between parameters of the synthesis process, the morphology of the composite material, and the corresponding effective properties.</p>
         
         <p>As shown in Ref. [9–13] for different electrode materials used in lithium ion batteries, 3D imaging with a subsequent analysis based on methods from spatial statistics and mathematical morphology<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0014_R_d118525043e453" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14">14</a>, <a href="#batt202300409-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0015_R_d118525043e453" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15">15</a></sup></span> is a powerful tool. It allows for quantitatively studying the nanostructure and their dependence on the synthesis process on the one hand and their impact on effective properties on the other hand. However, merely investigating experimental image data is limited due to the effort of sample preparation, image acquisition and analysis. This problem can be overcome by data-driven parametric stochastic 3D structure modeling, where virtual structures are generated that are statistically similar to the observed ones. By varying the parameters of the stochastic model, virtual structures can be simulated which exhibit different morphological properties than the structures reconstructed based on experimental imaging techniques. To mention two examples, the impact of calendering on the morphology of graphite anode electrodes<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0016_R_d118525043e456" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Comput. Mater. Sci.">16</a></sup></span> and structure-property-relationships of solid oxide fuel cell anodes (SOFC) anodes<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0017_R_d118525043e459" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - Comput. Mater. Sci.">17</a></sup></span> have been quantitatively explored with this methodology. Moreover, a stochastic structure model has been developed to generate virtual, but realistic nanostructured NMC particles<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0018_R_d118525043e462" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Int. J. Solids Struct.">18</a></sup></span> and has been used to study process-structure-property relationships of the latter.</p>
         
         <p>In the present paper, a stochastic 3D structure model for nanoporous NVP/C active material particles is calibrated based on image data aqcuired by focused ion beam (FIB) - scanning electron microscopy (SEM) tomography, FIB cross-sectioning, transmission electron microscopy (TEM) and energy-dispersive X-ray spectroscopy (EDX). A major challenge in electron microscopy of composite electrodes is the porous nature of the specimen which introduces imaging artefacts, e. g. shine-through artefacts and brightness variations due to the edge effect. This leads afterwards to a demanding analysis and segmentation of the obtained images. To cope with those difficulties an elaborate sample preparation, like embedding in epoxy or silicone resins to fill the pore space and thereby minimize imaging artefacts can be applied prior imaging<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0019_R_d118525043e468" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - Electrochem. Commun.">19</a></sup></span> or for instance algorithm-based segmentation approaches by optical flow estimations are deployed.<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0020_R_d118525043e471" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Ultramicroscopy">20</a></sup></span> Therefore, an embbeding approach with a silicone resin is used to fill the pore space and enhance contrast between the three phases, NVP, carbon and pore space. Further, to fine tune the segmentation of the detailed carbon and pore space additional high resolution SEM (HR-SEM) images are used. For underpinning of the information obtained by FIB-SEM and HR-SEM, further EDX and TEM measurements were performed. Since the considered nanostructure inside the active material particles consists of the three phases NVP, carbon and pores, the two-phase model for nanostructured NMC particles developed in<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0018_R_d118525043e474" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Int. J. Solids Struct.">18</a></sup></span> can not be applied. For modeling the three-phase nanostructure, we use the rather flexible Pluri-Gaussian model introduced in,<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0021_R_d118525043e477" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Comput. Mater. Sci.">21</a></sup></span> where we present a methodological framework to consistently combine the information from FIB-SEM and HR-SEM data. The model presented in Ref. [21] has the advantage that the parameters of the 3D model can be predicted based on 2D SEM data. Note that the required assumption of spatial isotropy is fulfilled in our case. The model is validated by means of morphological descriptors that have not been used for model calibration. Finally, the stochastic model is used for predictive simulation in order to quantify the effect of varying the amount of carbon while keeping the amount of NVP constant.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="batt202300409-sec-0002">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="batt202300409-sec-0002-title"> Materials and imaging</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="batt202300409-sec-0003">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="batt202300409-sec-0003-title"> Synthesis of nanostructured NVP/C particles</h3>
            
            <p>For the synthesis of the NVP/C-composite material, <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0004" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/be80f82d-93b6-4c30-bd8a-fe0d59f32c43/batt202300409-math-0004.png">
, <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0005" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/4fc7b877-e225-4561-82d5-907c3ef2dabb/batt202300409-math-0005.png">
 in molar ration of 4 : 6 : 3 were dissolved in water at <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0006" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/045e01ac-16cd-4294-b85d-ab9ee08be079/batt202300409-math-0006.png">
C. Lactose was added as carbon source with 18 mass %. The resulting solution was spray-dried with an inlet-temperature of <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0007" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/232de0cb-6f79-41c3-b757-4bd371530859/batt202300409-math-0007.png">
C and an outlet temperature of <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0008" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/34705a77-392a-4571-b27b-330e506b19e7/batt202300409-math-0008.png">
C. The so obtained precursor were calcined under an argon atmosphere. Hereby, the material was heated up to <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0009" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/3b7183de-1f9a-4a13-a892-00b7e7d42a2a/batt202300409-math-0009.png">
C with a heating rate of 1 K/min. Then the material was heated up to <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0010" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/c868d626-f1fd-4ebd-b2ec-b48b8d6bc403/batt202300409-math-0010.png">
C with a heating rate of 3 K/min and a subsequent dwell time of 5 h. Finally, the cooling was done with a cooling rate of 5 K/min to room temperature. This pre-calcined powder was ground in an agitator ball mill for 450 min at 3000 rpm with the use of <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0011" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/02ba7b70-f47f-4a5e-b27d-b1e52cb05e99/batt202300409-math-0011.png">
-milling balls (<img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0012" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/ac78e337-0ec8-4653-898b-5bb19d447b69/batt202300409-math-0012.png">
               <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0013" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/87897d99-58e6-403f-9e98-bab91eb3e3c2/batt202300409-math-0013.png">
 mm) in an aqueous suspension. Polyacrylic acid (PAA) (<img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0014" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/25f13709-14b3-4f71-a508-138f2d67fab5/batt202300409-math-0014.png">
=1800) and polyethylenglycol (PEG) was added to the suspension and it was spray-dried with same conditions. Finally, a second calcination step at <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0015" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/a58fe9e0-da71-4915-8095-1a59812f8fbc/batt202300409-math-0015.png">
C (dwell time=5 h, heating rate=3 K/min, atmosphere=<img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0016" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/333b8245-a606-44f7-9923-39ddd76efee1/batt202300409-math-0016.png">
 (97 : 3)) is done. Volume fractions of 0.556, 0.126, 0.318 are calculated for NVP, carbon and pores, respectively, based on the following values: specific pore volume of 0.162 cm<sup>3</sup>/g, carbon content of 10.5 wt%, a density of 2.88 g/cm<sup>3</sup> for the synthesized NVP/C composite, and a density of 3.16 g/cm<sup>3</sup> for the pure NVP phase.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="batt202300409-sec-0004">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="batt202300409-sec-0004-title"> Sample preparation for electron imaging</h3>
            
            <p>To enhance the contrast between the electrode components and the pore space during the imaging process, the pore space was infiltrated with a silicone resin (ELASTOSIL® RT601 A/B, Wacker Chemie AG, Germany). A small portion of the NVP/C composite electrode material was immersed into the resin and two vacuum steps were applied (5 min at 240 mbar, 5 min at ambient pressure, followed by 30 min at 240 mbar). Afterwards, the sample was removed from the resin and cured for 24 hours at ambient conditions. Subsequently, the sample was embedded in epoxy resin (EpoFix, Struers GmbH, Germany). The embedded electrode sample was exposed using SiC abrasive papers and the surface polished using diamond suspensions (monocrystalline, 3 μm and 1 μm, Leco Corporation, USA) on Nylon paper (Leco Corporation, USA). Finally, to avoid charging effects during electron imaging the samples were sputtered with an approx. 10 nm thick platinum layer.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="batt202300409-sec-0005">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="batt202300409-sec-0005-title"> FIB/SEM, TEM and EDX analysis</h3>
            
            <p>The FIB/SEM analysis was done with a Helios Nanolab 600 (Thermo Fisher Scientific Inc., USA) with a gallium ion beam operated at 30 kV and beam currents chosen accordingly. Protective platinum layers were deposited at the region of interest via ion beam induced deposition (IBID) using methylcyclopentadienyl trimethyl platinum (<img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0017" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/6e24303f-0fd1-4d4a-b362-7c8e172eb4d8/batt202300409-math-0017.png">
) as precursor prior cross-sectioning and FIB/SEM tomography. FIB/SEM tomography of a single particle of the active material was obtained using the “slice and view” software package (Thermo Fisher Scientific Inc., USA). Electron image acquisition was done at 3 kV and 86 pA using immersion mode and the through the lens detector (TLD) operated in backscattering electron (BSE) mode, electron images have a pixel size of <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0018" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/19b74a4d-4afa-4f9d-9b23-549f7660a87f/batt202300409-math-0018.png">
. For each image a slice of 20 nm thickness was removed at the front, 200 of these slices were done. For further phase identification and fine tuning of the segmentation algorithm, FIB/SEM cross-sectioning and HR-SEM imaging was done on another particle of the same active material. TLD BSE images were taken with 3 kV, 0.34 nA and a pixel size of <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0019" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/5136ec09-a055-4657-b27c-48c8029e619a/batt202300409-math-0019.png">
. In addition, a lamella with an average thickness of 130 nm was prepared from the same particle and transferred to a copper TEM grid using an OmniProbe manipulation needle (Oxford Instruments plc, GB) and platinum deposition via IBID. The TEM lamella was imaged using a TEM JEM-1400 (JEOL Ltd., Japan) operated at 120 kV. EDX mapping was done at the same lamella using a Quanta 3D FEG (Thermo Fisher Scientific Inc., USA) operated at 20 kV and 23 nA equipped with a SDD Apollo XV detector using the Genesis 6.5 acquisition software package (both EDAX Inc., Germany). For the element mapping a size of <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0020" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/e85aa0e0-a8ee-42a0-9913-6bbfc754269f/batt202300409-math-0020.png">
 pixel was chosen, pixel size was <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0021" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/3918dbd8-b2c8-41c7-837e-748516462626/batt202300409-math-0021.png">
 and the dwell time was 200 <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0022" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/939f3941-b275-4ac1-a8c9-c6bbef1680bb/batt202300409-math-0022.png">
 with 64 measured frames. The results of EDX measurements are provided as supplementary information, see Figure S1. In accordance with the EDX analysis the grayscale values in the SEM images can be allovcated as follows: high/bright indicates NVP, medium/gray indicates filled pore space, low/dark indicates the carbon domain.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="batt202300409-sec-0006">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="batt202300409-sec-0006-title"> Image segmentation</h3>
            
            <p>First, to segment the NVP phase in the image stack obtained by FIB/SEM tomography (exemplary cross-section is shown in Figure <a href="#batt202300409-fig-0002">2a</a>), the area of the NVP/C composite particle in the individual images is separated from its surroundings using the software package Ilastik.<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0022_R_d118525043e570" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22">22</a></sup></span> In short, a random forest classifier is trained using a few hand-labelled voxel and thereby, the area of the particle is separated from the rest of the image (Figure <a href="#batt202300409-fig-0002">2b</a>). Within this separated area a local Otsu threshold<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0023_R_d118525043e576" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - IEEE Trans. Syst. Man Cybern. Syst.">23</a></sup></span> is applied with a radius of <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0023" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/f5147461-234f-4e7a-83bb-5b6f18bb64d4/batt202300409-math-0023.png">
. This procedure is performed on each individual cross-section to compensate for brightness variations within the image stack. Afterwards, a majority filter using a <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0024" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/205d1328-2620-4da4-9d32-feb488bc867c/batt202300409-math-0024.png">
 voxel neighborhood was applied on the segmented image stack which leads to a smoothing between subsequent slices of the stack.</p>
            
            <p>Since the phase identfication between carbon and filled pore space is not unambiguous in the image stack obtained by FIB/SEM tomography, additional HR-SEM images of cross-sections were taken into account. Firstly, a median filter using a radius of 25 nm is applied for noise reduction and a local Otsu threshold<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0023_R_d118525043e587" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - IEEE Trans. Syst. Man Cybern. Syst.">23</a></sup></span> is used with a radius of <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0025" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/ced3b906-8d4b-4e39-a9da-fab0705acb62/batt202300409-math-0025.png">
 for segmentation of the NVP phase. In a second step, the complementary area of the image is further subdivided into carbon and filled pore space. Therefore, a <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0026" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/576b15a6-bf38-4e20-89e1-1560f2b85c27/batt202300409-math-0026.png">
 Mexican hat filter<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0024_R_d118525043e594" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Proc. R. Soc. London Ser. B">24</a></sup></span> is applied to enhance the contrast at the boundaries of the NVP phase to reduce a missclassification of medium high grayscale values, a usual problem in multi-phase image segmentation.<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0025_R_d118525043e597" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Water Resour. Res.">25</a></sup></span> Finally, an Otsu threshold<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0023_R_d118525043e601" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - IEEE Trans. Syst. Man Cybern. Syst.">23</a></sup></span> is applied with a radius of <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0027" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/e9fc0a33-c16f-48b3-9c06-3b2f650e1f81/batt202300409-math-0027.png">
 in this complement followed by a majority filter with a radius of 25 nm. This segmentation procedure leads to a good agreement between HR-SEM images and segmentation of the three phases (Figure 3a and 3b).</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="batt202300409-sec-0007">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="batt202300409-sec-0007-title"> Stochastic 3D modeling</h3>
            
            <p>The nanostructure consisting of the active material NVP, carbon and pores is modeled by a Pluri-Gaussian model, i. e., by excursion sets of Gaussian random fields.<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0014_R_d118525043e616" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14">14</a>, <a href="#batt202300409-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0026_R_d118525043e616" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26">26</a></sup></span> Excursion sets of Gaussian random fields are an appropriate model for the morphology of electrode materials.<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0017_R_d118525043e619" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - Comput. Mater. Sci.">17</a>, <a href="#batt202300409-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0021_R_d118525043e619" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Comput. Mater. Sci.">21</a>, <a href="#batt202300409-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0027_R_d118525043e619" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - J. Microsc.">27</a>, <a href="#batt202300409-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0028_R_d118525043e619" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Comput. Mater. Sci.">28</a></sup></span> In the present paper, we make use of the stochastic model described in Ref. [21]. The model is briefly described in Section 3.1. Model calibration to the image data, segmented as presented in Section 2.4., is performed in Section 3.2.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="batt202300409-sec-0008">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="batt202300409-sec-0008-title"> Model description</h3>
            
            <p>We consider two motion invariant, i. e., stationary and isotropic, Gaussian random fields <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0028" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/e149dbba-2884-4499-b367-ddca41fb1192/batt202300409-math-0028.png">
 and <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0029" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/7c5d42e4-369f-489a-be47-5efb6df26276/batt202300409-math-0029.png">
 which are centered and standardized. The latter means that the conditions <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0030" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/914791d7-0a08-43e3-9b64-75aad5bc4f4b/batt202300409-math-0030.png">
 and Var<img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0031" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/c744c1e1-ef94-4818-857e-c990985a1d86/batt202300409-math-0031.png">
 for the expectation and variance of the random variable <i>X</i>(<i>u</i>) are fulfilled for each <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0032" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/85af9564-1f61-4d6f-9e96-b4e4ab2caa6c/batt202300409-math-0032.png">
. Let <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0033" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/62d4ffe5-b88a-476b-8808-253c7c150e17/batt202300409-math-0033.png">
 denote the covariance functions of <i>X</i> and <i>Y</i>, i. e., <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0034" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/2f48e7dc-a485-4315-b53a-15863fb56761/batt202300409-math-0034.png">
 for all <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0035" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/f0bea7fe-ea51-47c0-87db-669586586588/batt202300409-math-0035.png">
 and analogous for <i>Y</i>. Note that by the motion invariance of <i>X</i> and <i>Y</i>, the values of their covariance functions at a pair <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0036" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/4763f1fb-7fa3-463d-b043-f3c517e700ce/batt202300409-math-0036.png">
 only depend on the distance <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0037" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/dc45ee52-c61e-4e98-9a50-48f48cd5d5f6/batt202300409-math-0037.png">
 for all <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0038" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/de82d3c0-15e1-45dc-b627-1eedb6f27401/batt202300409-math-0038.png">
. Hence, with some abuse of notation, we write <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0039" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/8045848e-8c2e-48c7-b64e-1fa08b83978d/batt202300409-math-0039.png">
 and <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0040" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/41dbff73-1cb1-4b1a-b925-1496c5b8c8f6/batt202300409-math-0040.png">
 for any <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0041" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/64422f9d-1c0b-435a-80af-707f7bff8443/batt202300409-math-0041.png">
, where <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0042" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/5951a9ca-ea6d-4a48-8b52-fd0114313fe8/batt202300409-math-0042.png">
 are arbitrary with <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0043" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/0fe53545-d3d6-4055-a52d-8cad267ade25/batt202300409-math-0043.png">
. By means of the random fields <i>X</i> and <i>Y</i>, we define a third random field <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0044" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/a96a5438-35cf-490e-8c7d-66951a42d69a/batt202300409-math-0044.png">
 by <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0045" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/f9148835-cba4-4f73-91a4-f39f98744f98/batt202300409-math-0045.png">
 for each <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0046" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/b5558df1-f57c-44f2-80b2-a7a702e89b99/batt202300409-math-0046.png">
 and some model parameter <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0047" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/32d8e27f-339f-4a84-83ff-aa6406ce02d2/batt202300409-math-0047.png">
 By construction, <i>Z</i> is also a motion-invariant, centered and standardized Gaussian random field. It inherits these properties from <i>X</i> and <i>Y</i>. Note that if <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0048" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/0362bc57-2a6d-496f-83a5-60fbef720034/batt202300409-math-0048.png">
, the random field <i>Z</i> coincides with <i>Y</i> and, thus, <i>X</i> and <i>Z</i> are independent. The closer the value of <i>m</i> is to 1, the stronger is the correlation between <i>X</i> and <i>Z</i> and in the extreme case <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0049" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/274eeae7-69bf-4315-a949-ce0232bd7836/batt202300409-math-0049.png">
, the random fields <i>X</i> and <i>Z</i> coincide.</p>
            
            <p>Based on the random fields <i>X</i> and <i>Z</i>, we construct random sets <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0050" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/25f59018-8d43-4ac8-b615-6303cd44315b/batt202300409-math-0050.png">
 and <i>Ξ</i><sub>3</sub>, which denote NVP, carbon, and pores, respectively. First, NVP is modeled as an excursion set of the random field <i>X</i>, namely <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0051" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/fd9e8bd5-ae4a-4654-82ce-a5491768307b/batt202300409-math-0051.png">
 for some parameter <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0052" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/a8c5773e-25f2-4aa1-92d4-ee044d133714/batt202300409-math-0052.png">
 In a second step, the remaining space is subdivided in carbon and pores with the random field <i>Z</i>. We define <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0053" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/ca284bcc-9c62-454c-a39b-6dfb021ddb24/batt202300409-math-0053.png">
 for some model parameter <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0054" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/2da5484e-5c07-4fa6-9767-00ff4af20e85/batt202300409-math-0054.png">
 The pore space <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0055" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/b134a95e-f42c-4c70-9cda-b44442cde46f/batt202300409-math-0055.png">
 is then given by complement of NVP and carbon. The model is uniquely determined by the two thresholds <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0056" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/5203ffc3-a23e-48b7-b6f7-a597d7322751/batt202300409-math-0056.png">
, the covariance functions <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0057" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/2178fb64-4460-4af3-ba7f-a0cb53ae52c7/batt202300409-math-0057.png">
 of the underlying Gaussian random fields <i>X, Y</i>, and the parameter <i>m</i>. By means of the two thresholds, the volume fractions of the two phases can be controlled, while the covariance functions strongly influence the shape of the phases. In particular, the faster the covariance functions decay, the finer is the morphology of the nanostructure in the model. The parameter <i>m</i> controls the dependence between the random fields <i>X</i> and <i>Z</i> and thus it influences the correlation between the phases Ξ<sub>1</sub> and Ξ<sub>2</sub>. For larger values of <i>m</i>, the accumulation of Ξ<sub>2</sub> around Ξ<sub>1</sub> is stronger, i. e., more carbon is accumulated close to the active material.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="batt202300409-sec-0009">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="batt202300409-sec-0009-title"> Model calibration</h3>
            
            <p>The model calibration is based on analytical relationships between morphological descriptors which can be estimated from image data on the one hand and the levels <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0058" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/5c5425ac-c743-426f-bd71-22503df3edb7/batt202300409-math-0058.png">
, the correlation functions <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0059" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/cf953728-92d9-4045-887a-a2cf22c220a8/batt202300409-math-0059.png">
 and the parameter <i>m</i> on the other hand. In the present paper, model calibration differs from the approach in<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0021_R_d118525043e792" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Comput. Mater. Sci.">21</a></sup></span> in the sense, that we use two different types of image data with different resolutions. More precisely, we use 3D image data obtained by FIB-SEM tomography with a voxel size of <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0060" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/60a8c8e7-c9a4-498f-a1c7-25506f127e1a/batt202300409-math-0060.png">
 to fit the covariance function <i>ρ<sub>X</sub></i> which determines the shape of the NVP phase. For calibrating the other parameters, which also require information about the spatial distribution of carbon and the pore space, we use the HR-SEM images with a pixel size of <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0061" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/b9b03532-9826-4f31-8bfb-0d9af2cbb673/batt202300409-math-0061.png">
.</p>
            
            <div class="paragraph-element">From image data, we estimate the volume fractions and the two-point coverage probability functions, see Section 3.1.6 in.<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0014_R_d118525043e807" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14">14</a></sup></span> The volume fraction <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0062" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/54efe51f-e680-4654-9d90-90d39ade220d/batt202300409-math-0062.png">
 of Ξ<sub><i>i</i></sub> is defined by
               <div class="inline-equation" id="batt202300409-disp-0001"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><img class="" src="/cms/asset/8516fa7c-0a2b-41ec-9601-e340e9be8056/batt202300409-math-0063.png" alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0063" title="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0063" loading="lazy"></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(1)</span></div>
               </div>
            
            <div class="paragraph-element">for each <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0064" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/41c7e00b-85a4-45f5-9f8f-a7f03fbf2206/batt202300409-math-0064.png">
, where <i>ν</i><sub>3</sub> denotes the three-dimensional Lebesgue measure and <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0065" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/a88ffe6c-e937-418e-8ca7-d3b56ac5d04f/batt202300409-math-0065.png">
 with <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0066" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/5fc6849c-404c-4057-98f2-4de76496dd46/batt202300409-math-0066.png">
 is an arbitrary sampling window. Note that in the case of stationarity, which is assumed for the nanostructures considered in the present paper, the definition of the volume fraction does not depend on the choice of <i>W</i>. To estimate the volume fractions from image data, we use the information from 3D FIB-SEM data to determine an estimator <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0067" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/6903da01-2ed7-48e0-bdb0-21f6230c22fc/batt202300409-math-0067.png">
 for the volume fraction <i>ϵ</i><sub>1</sub> of NVP by voxel counting. As described in Section 2.4., carbon can not be distinguished from the pore space in FIB-SEM data. Thus, to estimate the volume fraction of carbon and pores, we make use of the segmented HR-SEM images. Note that by voxel counting, volume fractions of a three-phase material can be estimated from cross-sections in an unbiased way, see Section 10.2.2 in.<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0014_R_d118525043e842" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14">14</a></sup></span> Doing so, we obtain the estimators <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0068" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/a1e2c2d5-43ba-4562-845d-3680124e74d7/batt202300409-math-0068.png">
 and <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0069" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/2f97435c-a637-4d09-8677-dfd9ac43c7de/batt202300409-math-0069.png">
 for <i>ϵ</i><sub>2</sub> and <i>ϵ</i><sub>3,</sub> respectively. For consistency, it is required that <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0070" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/c13653a0-d151-49d7-b677-31ff1e657ab6/batt202300409-math-0070.png">
. Thus, based on the 3D estimator for the volume fraction of NVP and the 2D estimators for the volume fraction of carbon and porosity, we define the final estimators <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0071" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/d5398697-269d-47c2-99ef-5c4fe99b8639/batt202300409-math-0071.png">
 and <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0072" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/2b2d6d0d-0405-435b-854a-3506c9c2e370/batt202300409-math-0072.png">
 for <i>ϵ</i><sub>2</sub> and <i>ϵ</i><sub>3</sub> by
               <div class="inline-equation" id="batt202300409-disp-0002"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><img class="" src="/cms/asset/0924dac8-7620-4054-b532-b135f638dfbc/batt202300409-math-0073.png" alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0073" title="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0073" loading="lazy"></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(2)</span></div>
               </div>
            
            <div class="paragraph-element">and
               <div class="inline-equation" id="batt202300409-disp-0003"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><img class="" src="/cms/asset/02453af4-ca16-40b9-9177-4d45d7a754df/batt202300409-math-0074.png" alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0074" title="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0074" loading="lazy"></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(3)</span></div>
               </div>
            
            <p>This means that we complement the information from 3D image data with the information regarding the ratio of volume fraction of carbon and of porosity. Thereby, we obtain <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0075" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/47a9ef57-bb7c-4fcd-b45f-8dec2d22407a/batt202300409-math-0075.png">
, and <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0076" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/85152f19-ff62-4238-b244-46dd0885a728/batt202300409-math-0076.png">
. The estimated volume fraction of NVP is in good accordance with the determined value in Section 2.1. The slight underestimation can be attributed to the fact that we consider a cutout from the inner structure of an NVP/C particle and the volume fraction of NVP is larger at the boundary, see Figure <a href="#batt202300409-fig-0001">1</a>. The mismatch between the estimated volume fractions of carbon and pores compared to the values in Section 2.1. arises due to possible small nanopores which are not resolved in the segmentation of HR-SEM images as observed in TEM data, the visualization of which is provided as supplementary information, see Figure S7. Thus, when speaking about the carbon phase, we mean the carbon phase including small nanopores. When discussing the influence of the volume fraction of carbon on the morphology of NVP/C particles in Section 4.2., we provide a formula to recompute the mere volume fraction of carbon based on the volume fraction of carbon including the small nanopores. The latter is reflected in <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0077" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/cc218979-ffc9-4733-8ccd-87d048c54964/batt202300409-math-0077.png">
               </p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="batt202300409-fig-0001"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/f6bdd0cf-f3e2-47fb-9043-859fe1203922/batt202300409-fig-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/f6bdd0cf-f3e2-47fb-9043-859fe1203922/batt202300409-fig-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/9c110d0a-1ca6-4a0e-a0f8-d7dc4f7ac091/batt202300409-fig-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/f6bdd0cf-f3e2-47fb-9043-859fe1203922/batt202300409-fig-0001-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=batt202300409-fig-0001&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fbatt.202300409" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">
                        <p>BSE image of a cross-section of a NVP/C composite particle (a), area of the NVP/C particle extracted from the BSE image in white using the software Ilastik (b) and the segmented NVP phase (white, c).</p></div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            
            <div class="paragraph-element">In addition to the volume fractions of phase, we use the two-point coverage probability functions <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0078" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/f6ee16d1-0c5b-4d59-a645-d7758d651b2b/batt202300409-math-0078.png">
 defined by
               <div class="inline-equation" id="batt202300409-disp-0004"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><img class="" src="/cms/asset/c634911d-f2fe-4ea7-a061-15467b92b3c6/batt202300409-math-0079.png" alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0079" title="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0079" loading="lazy"></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(4)</span></div>
               </div>
            
            <div class="paragraph-element">for <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0080" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/f37fa4a8-92a7-460d-8889-3412750b68f8/batt202300409-math-0080.png">
 and each <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0081" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/d4c5bdd9-cd0c-484d-a663-2271e49d470f/batt202300409-math-0081.png">
 where <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0082" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/1c58fbf5-7d88-48cd-ad5a-2b2b11f33d25/batt202300409-math-0082.png">
 such that <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0083" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/6d341ccd-ddda-47c4-9018-69e4b4fe3991/batt202300409-math-0083.png">
. Note that due to the assumption of stationarity and isotropy, the values of <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0084" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/603e0333-d3c1-4d5f-841c-c13f9b9993c2/batt202300409-math-0084.png">
 do not depend on the particular choice of <i>s</i> and <i>t</i>. The two-point coverage probabilities indicate spatial dependencies within the considered structure. If the phases at locations having a distance <i>h</i> between each other are independent, then
               <div class="inline-equation" id="batt202300409-disp-0005"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><img class="" src="/cms/asset/293c93a6-9e3f-4677-a473-4c1446f34ade/batt202300409-math-0085.png" alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0085" title="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0085" loading="lazy"></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(5)</span></div>
               </div>
            
            <p>where the latter equality follows from Equation (6.34) in.<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0014_R_d118525043e963" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14">14</a></sup></span> Provided that <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0086" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/150abd3c-7f0b-4a1b-9241-36d677731e0b/batt202300409-math-0086.png">
, then it is more likely that a predefined point belongs to the <i>i</i>th phase if there is another point with distance <i>h</i> that belongs to the <i>j</i>th phase. An analogous statement can be made if <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0087" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/1c1078c4-6314-49f7-aa18-26b0ec02a185/batt202300409-math-0087.png">
 For computing estimators <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0088" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/26c6f4f3-27a4-4241-b657-8af04b3f06cf/batt202300409-math-0088.png">
 for the two-point coverage probability functions <i>C<sub>ij</sub></i> for all <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0089" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/9b2d6341-1a16-4051-b503-b2d4e0e128fb/batt202300409-math-0089.png">
 from image data, we use the algorithm described in Section 6.2 of<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0029_R_d118525043e985" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29">29</a></sup></span> which is based on the fast Fourier transformation. We estimate <i>C</i><sub>11</sub>, i. e., the two-point coverage probability function of NVP based on all FIB-SEM cross-sections, while the other functions <i>C<sub>ij</sub></i> with <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0090" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/6bade2c0-a707-4440-82dd-3af8ca6e0842/batt202300409-math-0090.png">
 are estimated based on the HR-SEM images, for which a three-phase segmentation is possible.</p>
            
            <div class="paragraph-element">Based on this information contained in the volume fractions and the two-point coverage probability functions, the model parameters are estimated. First, the model parameter <i>λ<sub>X</sub></i> is estimated using the relationship <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0091" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/d344ec90-7ef9-444c-aa7d-de6fb52028f8/batt202300409-math-0091.png">
 see Equation (6.157) in [14] i. e., the estimator <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0092" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/10767921-ed06-4be6-a2cd-2cf6f796caa3/batt202300409-math-0092.png">
 for <i>λ<sub>X</sub></i> is given by
               <div class="inline-equation" id="batt202300409-disp-0006"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><img class="" src="/cms/asset/e908acf9-dde6-485d-b61a-b6d80507c499/batt202300409-math-0093.png" alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0093" title="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0093" loading="lazy"></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(6)</span></div>
               </div>
            
            <div class="paragraph-element">where Φ denotes the probability distribution function of the standard normal distribution. Furthermore, for all <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0094" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/4efa922b-28d2-4588-8d8e-6e28c7877495/batt202300409-math-0094.png">
, let <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0095" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/6daffec1-43cf-4c77-a1dd-d0d0c97d937e/batt202300409-math-0095.png">
 denote the bivariate probability density function of a two-dimensional Gaussian random vector evaluated at <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0096" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/b615b1df-51b4-446d-8fad-006aeafc4a87/batt202300409-math-0096.png">
, where the marginal distributions are standard normal and the correlation coefficient is <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0097" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/5e946c96-bb63-4779-be81-e84a891cda3f/batt202300409-math-0097.png">
 With the estimator <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0098" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/68bc3a24-44c5-4cd4-b622-c0ee316f3933/batt202300409-math-0098.png">
 for <i>C</i><sub>11</sub>, we determine a non-parametric estimator <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0099" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/a84bcbb7-4be4-409b-9242-0d69cef7f711/batt202300409-math-0099.png">
 for <i>ρ<sub>X</sub></i> by means of the relationship
               <div class="inline-equation" id="batt202300409-disp-0007"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><img class="" src="/cms/asset/b7710c72-3312-4941-8d90-99e4deadbc45/batt202300409-math-0100.png" alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0100" title="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0100" loading="lazy"></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(7)</span></div>
               </div>
            
            <div class="paragraph-element">which is valid for each <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0101" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/6f6ab679-1928-4a77-a3c4-c8477573789f/batt202300409-math-0101.png">
. Considering <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0102" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/7a9d751c-82aa-48b0-a7e3-fb11c01f75fb/batt202300409-math-0102.png">
, it turns out that
               <div class="inline-equation" id="batt202300409-disp-0008"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><img class="" src="/cms/asset/2d028475-59dd-4f51-8829-8e1e823b812a/batt202300409-math-0103.png" alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0103" title="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0103" loading="lazy"></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(8)</span></div>
               </div>
            
            <p>is an appropriate model for the correlation function of the random field <i>X</i>. The estimator <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0104" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/4a3c8c36-92dc-4694-b7b3-cc78af597699/batt202300409-math-0104.png">
 for the parameter <i>α<sub>X</sub></i> is determined via the method of least squares.</p>
            
            <div class="paragraph-element">For estimating the remaining parameters, we make use of the following analytical relationships derived in,<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0021_R_d118525043e1079" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Comput. Mater. Sci.">21</a></sup></span> where <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0105" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/e22df6fd-77ed-445e-9723-8ae42c7889db/batt202300409-math-0105.png">
 denotes the density of the standard normal distribution evaluated at <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0106" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/47b3be20-7299-46e2-9cb4-200d396c4047/batt202300409-math-0106.png">
. The first, which reads as
               <div class="inline-equation" id="batt202300409-disp-0009"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><img class="" src="/cms/asset/c02b4499-5a8b-4ba5-8c3c-1fbb05156e93/batt202300409-math-0107.png" alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0107" title="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0107" loading="lazy"></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(9)</span></div>
               </div>
            
            <div class="paragraph-element">related the volume fraction of the carbon phase to the model parameters <i>λ<sub>Z</sub></i> and <i>m</i>. The second and the third, given by
               <div class="inline-equation" id="batt202300409-disp-0010"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><img class="" src="/cms/asset/545e3abc-afae-4b83-b47e-77fd7fa6fa6c/batt202300409-math-0108.png" alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0108" title="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0108" loading="lazy"></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(10)</span></div>
               </div>
            
            <div class="paragraph-element">And
               <div class="inline-equation" id="batt202300409-disp-0011"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><img class="" src="/cms/asset/b5004ce9-e210-4438-8ab7-3628c62027cc/batt202300409-math-0109.png" alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0109" title="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0109" loading="lazy"></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(11)</span></div>
               </div>
            
            <div class="paragraph-element">for each <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0110" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/9bdef1bc-b116-4a20-888e-2faf9b396731/batt202300409-math-0110.png">
, relate the covariance functions <i>ρ<sub>X</sub></i> and <i>ρ<sub>Y</sub></i> of the random fields <i>X</i> and <i>Y</i> as well as the parameter <i>m</i> to the two-point coverage probability functions <i>C</i><sub>22</sub> and <i>C</i><sub>12</sub>. Then, we fix the parameter <i>m</i>, and compute an estimator <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0111" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/bdebd7aa-cc43-4d1b-acbf-1ba0bb37f597/batt202300409-math-0111.png">
 for <i>λ<sub>Z</sub></i> by Equation (9). Here we plug in <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0112" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/f60170e4-1e71-41c3-8fe7-3321dc832ce8/batt202300409-math-0112.png">
, which is obtained by Equation&nbsp;(6), for <i>λ</i><sub><i>X</i>.</sub> In a further step, we plug in the estimators <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0113" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/276cd9a6-05e1-4d90-be04-02d0c6f4f3ae/batt202300409-math-0113.png">
 and the non-parametric estimator <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0114" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/5308aabf-9bc1-4d8a-a38a-695140dd6ea3/batt202300409-math-0114.png">
, computed by means of Equation (7), into Equation (10). Doing so, a non-parameteric estimator <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0115" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/3174f51c-e6c2-40ee-98b9-ea5fc07b93dc/batt202300409-math-0115.png">
 for <i>ρ<sub>Y</sub></i> is determined. Having estimated all the parameters for each fixed <i>m</i> in the range of <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0116" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/26f79c6f-e03c-4bff-8a61-3d327915a454/batt202300409-math-0116.png">
 we plugin the obtained estimators into Equation (11) and minimize the distance between the right-hand side of Equation (11) and the estimator <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0117" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/d141c5de-aaa6-47bb-9043-e6a366a2a929/batt202300409-math-0117.png">
 computed from image data. For numerical details of the described computation of estimators, we refer to Section 3 in.<span><sup><a href="#batt202300409-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="batt202300409-bib-0021_R_d118525043e1179" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Comput. Mater. Sci.">21</a></sup></span> Considering the final non-parameteric estimator <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0118" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/c3fb50d5-d65c-4183-8a95-5fd5d3a4be46/batt202300409-math-0118.png">
, it is suitable to assume
               <div class="inline-equation" id="batt202300409-disp-0012"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><img class="" src="/cms/asset/1e6818a5-5793-4d00-b464-b631979f3b84/batt202300409-math-0119.png" alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0119" title="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0119" loading="lazy"></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(12)</span></div>
               </div>
            
            <p>for each <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0120" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/50439e19-d85d-464b-8003-b726e935d0a4/batt202300409-math-0120.png">
, where <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0121" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/82e60b74-b9df-4756-912c-553137bf000e/batt202300409-math-0121.png">
 is a model parameter. As in the case of <i>α<sub>X</sub></i>, an estimator <img alt="urn:x-wiley:25666223:media:batt202300409:batt202300409-math-0122" loading="lazy" class="section_image" src="/cms/asset/8fbb7c69-d953-4d44-b8b4-2878435cd1bf/batt202300409-math-0122.png">
 for <i>α<sub>Y</sub></i> is computed by the method of least-squares. The values of the computed estimators are provided in Table <a class="tableLink scrollableLink" title="Link to table" href="#batt202300409-tbl-0001">1</a>.
</p>
            
            <div class="article-table-content" id="batt202300409-tbl-0001">
